class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">Website</th><td>\n<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nato.int/">NATO.int</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>North Atlantic Treaty Organization</b> (<b>NATO</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Organisation du Trait\xc3\xa9 de l\'Atlantique Nord</i>; <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">OTAN</i></i>), also called the <b>North Atlantic Alliance</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_alliance" title="Military alliance">military alliance</a> between 29 North American and European countries. The organization implements the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a> that was signed on 4 April 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> NATO constitutes a system of <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">collective defence</a> whereby its independent member states agree to mutual defence in response to an attack by any external party. NATO Headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Haren,_Belgium" title="Haren, Belgium">Haren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Powers_Europe" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe">headquarters of Allied Command Operations</a> is near <a href="/wiki/Mons" title="Mons">Mons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>.\n</p><p>Since its founding, the admission of new member states has increased the alliance from the original 12 countries to 29. The most recent <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO" title="Enlargement of NATO">member state to be added</a> to NATO is <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> on 5 June 2017. NATO currently recognizes <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> as aspiring members.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> An additional 21&#160;countries participate in NATO\'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> program, with 15&#160;other countries involved in institutionalized dialogue programs. The combined military spending of all NATO members constitutes over 70% of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">the global total</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sipri1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sipri1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Members have committed to reach or maintain defense spending of at least 2% of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> by 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT_spending_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_spending-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_NATO" title="History of NATO">History of NATO</a></div>\n<p>On 4 March 1947 the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Dunkirk" title="Treaty of Dunkirk">Treaty of Dunkirk</a> was signed by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> as a <i>Treaty of Alliance and Mutual Assistance</i> in the event of a possible attack by Germany or the Soviet Union in the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. In 1948, this alliance was expanded to include the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> countries, in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Union_(alliance)" title="Western Union (alliance)">Western Union</a>, also referred to as the Brussels Treaty Organization (BTO), established by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Talks for a new military alliance which could also include North America resulted in the signature of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a> on 4 April 1949 by the member states of the Western Union plus the United States, Canada, Portugal, Italy, Norway, Denmark and Iceland.<sup id="cite_ref-history_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The North Atlantic Treaty was largely dormant until the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> initiated the establishment of NATO to implement it, by means of an integrated military structure: This included the formation of <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Powers_Europe" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe">Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe</a> (SHAPE) in 1951, which adopted the Western Union\'s military structures and plans.<sup id="cite_ref-pace_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pace-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1952 the post of <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_NATO" title="Secretary General of NATO">Secretary General of NATO</a> was established as the organization\'s chief civilian, the first major NATO <a href="/wiki/Military_exercise" title="Military exercise">maritime exercises</a> began; <a href="/wiki/Exercise_Mainbrace" title="Exercise Mainbrace">Exercise Mainbrace</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> acceded.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 1955 <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> was also incorporated into NATO, which resulted in the creation of the Soviet-dominated <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>, delineating the two opposing sides of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.\n</p><p>Doubts over the strength of the relationship between the European states and the United States ebbed and flowed, along with doubts over the credibility of the NATO defense against a prospective <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> invasion \xe2\x80\x93 doubts that led to the development of the <a href="/wiki/Strike_Force_(France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Strike Force (France)">independent French nuclear deterrent</a> and the withdrawal of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> from NATO\'s military structure in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEvan_der_Eyden2003104\xe2\x80\x93106_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEvan_der_Eyden2003104\xe2\x80\x93106-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WP-France_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-France-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1982 the newly democratic Spain joined the alliance.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">collapse</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> in 1989-1991 removed the <i>de facto</i> main adversary of NATO and caused a strategic re-evaluation of NATO\'s purpose, nature, tasks, and their focus on the continent of Europe. This shift started with the 1990 signing in Paris of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a> between NATO and the Soviet Union, which mandated specific military reductions across the continent that continued after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in December 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> At that time, European countries accounted for 34 percent of NATO\'s military spending; by 2012, this had fallen to 21 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> NATO also began a gradual expansion to include newly autonomous <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern European</a> nations, and extended its activities into political and humanitarian situations that had not formerly been NATO concerns.\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Berlin_Wall" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of the Berlin Wall">fall of the Berlin Wall</a> in Germany in 1989, the organization conducted its first <a href="/wiki/List_of_NATO_operations" title="List of NATO operations">military interventions</a> in <a href="/wiki/NATO_intervention_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="NATO intervention in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia from 1992 to 1995</a> and later <a href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia in 1999</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  Politically, the organization sought better relations with former Warsaw Pact countries, most of which joined the alliance in 1999 and 2004. <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty#Article_5" class="extiw" title="s:North Atlantic Treaty">Article&#160;5 of the North Atlantic treaty</a>, requiring member states to come to the aid of any member state subject to an armed attack, was invoked for the first and only time after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> after which troops were deployed to <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> under the NATO-led <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">ISAF</a>. The organization has operated a range of additional roles since then, including sending <a href="/wiki/NATO_Training_Mission_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="NATO Training Mission \xe2\x80\x93 Iraq">trainers to Iraq</a>, assisting in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ocean_Shield" title="Operation Ocean Shield">counter-piracy operations</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and in 2011 enforcing a <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">no-fly zone</a> <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">over Libya</a> in accordance with <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973">UN Security Council Resolution 1973</a>. The less potent Article 4, which merely invokes consultation among NATO members, has been invoked five times following incidents in the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a>.\n</p><p>The first post-Cold War expansion of NATO came with <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> on 3 October 1990, when the former <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> became part of the Federal Republic of Germany and the alliance. As part of post-Cold War restructuring, NATO\'s military structure was cut back and reorganized, with new forces such as the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Rapid_Reaction_Corps" title="Allied Rapid Reaction Corps">Headquarters Allied Command Europe Rapid Reaction Corps</a> established. The changes brought about by the collapse of the Soviet Union on the military balance in Europe were recognized in the <a href="/wiki/Adapted_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe_Treaty" title="Adapted Conventional Armed Forces in Europe Treaty">Adapted Conventional Armed Forces in Europe Treaty</a>, which was signed in 1999. The policies of French President <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> resulted in a major reform of France\'s military position, culminating with the return to full membership on 4 April 2009, which also included France rejoining the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Military_Command_Structure" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Military Command Structure">NATO Military Command Structure</a>, while maintaining an independent nuclear deterrent.<sup id="cite_ref-WP-France_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-France-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-france_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-france-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DPC_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DPC-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1994 and 1997, wider forums for regional cooperation between NATO and its neighbors were set up, like the <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Dialogue" title="Mediterranean Dialogue">Mediterranean Dialogue</a> initiative and the <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a>. In 1998, the <a href="/wiki/NATO%E2%80%93Russia_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO\xe2\x80\x93Russia relations">NATO\xe2\x80\x93Russia Permanent Joint Council</a> was established. Between 1999 and 2017 NATO incorporated the following Central and Eastern European countries, including several former communist states: the Czech Republic, Hungary, Poland, Bulgaria, Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania, Romania, Slovakia, Slovenia, Albania, Croatia and Montenegro.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">Russian intervention in Crimea</a> in 2014 lead to strong condemnation by NATO nations and the creation of a new "spearhead" force of 5,000 troops at bases in Estonia, Lithuania, Latvia, Poland, Romania, and Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> At the subsequent <a href="/wiki/2014_Wales_summit" title="2014 Wales summit">2014 Wales summit</a>, the leaders of NATO\'s member states formally committed for the first time spend the equivalent of at least 2% of their <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic products</a> on defence by 2024, which had previously been only an informal guideline.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_operations">Military operations</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_NATO_operations" title="List of NATO operations">List of NATO operations</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_operations">Early operations</span></h3>\n<p>No military operations were conducted by NATO during the Cold War. Following the end of the Cold War, the first operations, <i>Anchor Guard</i> in 1990 and <i>Ace Guard</i> in 1991, were prompted by the Iraqi <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">invasion of Kuwait</a>. Airborne early warning aircraft were sent to provide coverage of southeastern Turkey, and later a quick-reaction force was deployed to the area.<sup id="cite_ref-NATO_Operations_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NATO_Operations-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_intervention">Bosnia and Herzegovina intervention</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NATO_intervention_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="NATO intervention in Bosnia and Herzegovina">NATO intervention in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:F-16_deliberate_force.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A fighter jet with AV marked on its tail takes off from a mountain runway." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/F-16_deliberate_force.JPG/220px-F-16_deliberate_force.JPG" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/F-16_deliberate_force.JPG/330px-F-16_deliberate_force.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/F-16_deliberate_force.JPG/440px-F-16_deliberate_force.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:F-16_deliberate_force.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NATO planes engaged in aerial bombardments during <a href="/wiki/1995_NATO_bombing_campaign_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="1995 NATO bombing campaign in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Operation <i>Deliberate Force</i></a> after the <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre" title="Srebrenica massacre">Srebrenica massacre</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a> began in 1992, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a>. The deteriorating situation led to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_816" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 816">United Nations Security Council Resolution 816</a> on 9 October 1992, ordering a <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">no-fly zone</a> over central Bosnia and Herzegovina, which NATO began enforcing on 12 April 1993 with <a href="/wiki/Operation_Deny_Flight" title="Operation Deny Flight">Operation <i>Deny Flight</i></a>. From June 1993 until October 1996, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sharp_Guard" title="Operation Sharp Guard">Operation <i>Sharp Guard</i></a> added maritime enforcement of the <a href="/wiki/Arms_embargo" title="Arms embargo">arms embargo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_sanctions" title="Economic sanctions">economic sanctions</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. On 28 February 1994, NATO took its first wartime action by <a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka_incident" title="Banja Luka incident">shooting down four Bosnian Serb aircraft</a> violating the no-fly zone.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZenko2010133\xe2\x80\x93134_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZenko2010133\xe2\x80\x93134-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 and 11 April 1994, during the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Protection_Force" title="United Nations Protection Force">United Nations Protection Force</a> called in air strikes to protect the <a href="/wiki/Gora%C5%BEde" title="Gora\xc5\xbede">Gora\xc5\xbede</a> safe area, resulting in the bombing of a Bosnian Serb military command outpost near Gora\xc5\xbede by two US <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16</a> jets acting under NATO direction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZenko2010134_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZenko2010134-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This resulted in the taking of 150&#160;U.N. personnel hostage on 14 April.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On 16 April a British <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_Sea_Harrier" title="British Aerospace Sea Harrier">Sea Harrier</a> was shot down over Gora\xc5\xbede by Serb forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethlehemWeller1997liiv_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethlehemWeller1997liiv-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> A two-week NATO bombing campaign, <a href="/wiki/1995_NATO_bombing_campaign_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="1995 NATO bombing campaign in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Operation <i>Deliberate Force</i></a>, began in August 1995 against the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Republika_Srpska" class="mw-redirect" title="Army of the Republika Srpska">Army of the Republika Srpska</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre" title="Srebrenica massacre">Srebrenica massacre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-zenko137_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zenko137-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>NATO air strikes that year helped bring the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav wars">Yugoslav wars</a> to an end, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Agreement</a> in November 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-zenko137_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zenko137-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> As part of this agreement, NATO deployed a UN-mandated peacekeeping force, under <a href="/wiki/Operation_Joint_Endeavor" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Joint Endeavor">Operation <i>Joint Endeavor</i></a>, named <a href="/wiki/IFOR" class="mw-redirect" title="IFOR">IFOR</a>. Almost 60,000 NATO troops were joined by forces from non-NATO nations in this peacekeeping mission. This transitioned into the smaller <a href="/wiki/SFOR" class="mw-redirect" title="SFOR">SFOR</a>, which started with 32,000 troops initially and ran from December 1996 until December 2004, when operations were then passed onto <a href="/wiki/EUFOR_Althea" class="mw-redirect" title="EUFOR Althea">European Union Force Althea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClausson200694\xe2\x80\x9397_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClausson200694\xe2\x80\x9397-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Following the lead of its member nations, NATO began to award a service medal, the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Medal" title="NATO Medal">NATO Medal</a>, for these operations.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kosovo_intervention">Kosovo intervention</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo,_summer_1999.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Three trucks of soldiers idle on a country road in front of trees and red roofed houses. The rear truck has KFOR painted on is back." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo%2C_summer_1999.jpg/220px-German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo%2C_summer_1999.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo%2C_summer_1999.jpg/330px-German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo%2C_summer_1999.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo%2C_summer_1999.jpg/440px-German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo%2C_summer_1999.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2280" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_KFOR_troops_patrol_southern_Kosovo,_summer_1999.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German KFOR soldiers patrol southern Kosovo in 1999.</div></div></div>\n<p>In an effort to stop <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milo\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87">Slobodan Milo\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87</a>\'s Serbian-led crackdown on <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Liberation_Army" title="Kosovo Liberation Army">KLA</a> separatists and Albanian civilians in Kosovo, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1199" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1199">Resolution 1199</a> on 23 September 1998 to demand a ceasefire. Negotiations under US Special Envoy <a href="/wiki/Richard_Holbrooke" title="Richard Holbrooke">Richard Holbrooke</a> broke down on 23 March 1999, and he handed the matter to NATO,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> which started a 78-day bombing campaign on 24 March 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Operation <i>Allied Force</i> targeted the military capabilities of what was then the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. During the crisis, NATO also deployed one of its international reaction forces, the <a href="/wiki/ACE_Mobile_Force_(Land)" class="mw-redirect" title="ACE Mobile Force (Land)">ACE Mobile Force (Land)</a>, to Albania as the Albania Force (AFOR), to deliver humanitarian aid to refugees from Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-gs_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gs-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Though the campaign was criticized for <a href="/wiki/Civilian_casualties_during_Operation_Allied_Force" title="Civilian casualties during Operation Allied Force">high civilian casualties</a>, including bombing of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._bombing_of_the_Chinese_embassy_in_Belgrade" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. bombing of the Chinese embassy in Belgrade">Chinese embassy in Belgrade</a>, Milo\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87 finally accepted the terms of an international peace plan on 3 June 1999, ending the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>. On 11 June, Milo\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87 further accepted <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1244" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1244">UN resolution 1244</a>, under the mandate of which NATO then helped establish the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a> peacekeeping force. Nearly one million refugees had fled Kosovo, and part of KFOR\'s mandate was to protect the humanitarian missions, in addition to deterring violence.<sup id="cite_ref-gs_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gs-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In August\xe2\x80\x93September 2001, the alliance also mounted <a href="/wiki/Operation_Essential_Harvest" title="Operation Essential Harvest">Operation <i>Essential Harvest</i></a>, a mission disarming ethnic Albanian militias in the Republic of Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> As of  1&#160;December&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=NATO&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 4,882&#160;KFOR soldiers, representing 31&#160;countries, continue to operate in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The US, the UK, and most other NATO countries opposed efforts to require the UN Security Council to approve NATO military strikes, such as the action against Serbia in 1999, while France and some others claimed that the alliance needed UN approval.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The US/UK side claimed that this would undermine the authority of the alliance, and they noted that Russia and China would have exercised their Security Council vetoes to block the strike on <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, and could do the same in future conflicts where NATO intervention was required, thus nullifying the entire potency and purpose of the organization. Recognizing the post-Cold War military environment, NATO adopted the Alliance Strategic Concept during its <a href="/wiki/1999_Washington_summit" title="1999 Washington summit">Washington summit</a> in April 1999 that emphasized conflict prevention and crisis management.<sup id="cite_ref-nato.int_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nato.int-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_in_Afghanistan">War in Afghanistan</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">International Security Assistance Force</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932014)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Afghanistan (2001\xe2\x80\x932014)">War in Afghanistan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Park_Service_9-11_Statue_of_Liberty_and_WTC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A monumental green copper statue of a woman with a torch stands on an island in front of a mainland where a massive plume of gray smoke billows amongst skyscrapers." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/National_Park_Service_9-11_Statue_of_Liberty_and_WTC.jpg/220px-National_Park_Service_9-11_Statue_of_Liberty_and_WTC.jpg" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/National_Park_Service_9-11_Statue_of_Liberty_and_WTC.jpg/330px-National_Park_Service_9-11_Statue_of_Liberty_and_WTC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2f/National_Park_Service_9-11_Statue_of_Liberty_and_WTC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="385" data-file-height="315" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Park_Service_9-11_Statue_of_Liberty_and_WTC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> in the United States caused NATO to invoke its collective defence article for the first time.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> in the United States caused NATO to invoke Article&#160;5 of the NATO Charter for the first time in the organization\'s history. The Article says that an attack on any member shall be considered to be an attack on all. The invocation was confirmed on 4 October 2001 when NATO determined that the attacks were indeed eligible under the terms of the North Atlantic Treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The eight official actions taken by NATO in response to the attacks included <a href="/wiki/Operation_Eagle_Assist" title="Operation Eagle Assist">Operation <i>Eagle Assist</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Active_Endeavour" title="Operation Active Endeavour">Operation <i>Active Endeavour</i></a>, a naval operation in the Mediterranean Sea which is designed to prevent the movement of terrorists or weapons of mass destruction, as well as enhancing the security of shipping in general which began on 4 October 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The alliance showed unity: On 16 April 2003, NATO agreed to take command of the <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">International Security Assistance Force</a> (ISAF), which includes troops from 42 countries. The decision came at the request of Germany and the Netherlands, the two nations leading ISAF at the time of the agreement, and all nineteen NATO ambassadors approved it unanimously. The handover of control to NATO took place on 11 August, and marked the first time in NATO\'s history that it took charge of a mission outside the north Atlantic area.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A general hands a NATO flag from a soldier on the left to one on the right." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg/220px-Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg/330px-Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg/440px-Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodriguez_at_Italian_command_change_in_Herat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ISAF General <a href="/wiki/David_M._Rodriguez" title="David M. Rodriguez">David M. Rodriguez</a> at an Italian change of command in <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a></div></div></div>\n<p>ISAF was initially charged with securing <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a> and surrounding areas from the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Qaeda" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qaeda">al Qaeda</a> and factional warlords, so as to allow for the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Transitional_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Afghan Transitional Administration">Afghan Transitional Administration</a> headed by <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Karzai" title="Hamid Karzai">Hamid Karzai</a>. In October 2003, the UN Security Council authorized the expansion of the ISAF mission throughout Afghanistan,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and ISAF subsequently expanded the mission in four main stages over the whole of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-ISAF_Chronology_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISAF_Chronology-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 July 2006, the ISAF additionally took over <a href="/wiki/Coalition_combat_operations_in_Afghanistan_in_2006" title="Coalition combat operations in Afghanistan in 2006">military operations in the south of Afghanistan</a> from a US-led anti-terrorism coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Due to the intensity of the fighting in the south, in 2011 France allowed a squadron of <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_2000" title="Dassault Mirage 2000">Mirage 2000</a> fighter/attack aircraft to be moved into the area, to <a href="/wiki/Kandahar_International_Airport" title="Kandahar International Airport">Kandahar</a>, in order to reinforce the alliance\'s efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> During its <a href="/wiki/2012_Chicago_Summit" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Chicago Summit">2012 Chicago Summit</a>, NATO endorsed a plan to end the Afghanistan war and to remove the NATO-led ISAF Forces by the end of December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_20120521_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_20120521-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> ISAF was disestablished in December 2014 and replaced by the follow-on training <a href="/wiki/Resolute_Support_Mission" title="Resolute Support Mission">Resolute Support Mission</a>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq_training_mission">Iraq training mission</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NATO_Training_Mission_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="NATO Training Mission \xe2\x80\x93 Iraq">NATO Training Mission \xe2\x80\x93 Iraq</a></div>\n<p>In August 2004, during the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>, NATO formed the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Training_Mission_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="NATO Training Mission \xe2\x80\x93 Iraq">NATO Training Mission \xe2\x80\x93 Iraq</a>, a training mission to assist the Iraqi security forces in conjunction with the US led <a href="/wiki/Multinational_Force_%E2%80%93_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Multinational Force \xe2\x80\x93 Iraq">MNF-I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The NATO Training Mission-Iraq (NTM-I) was established at the request of the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Interim_Government" title="Iraqi Interim Government">Iraqi Interim Government</a> under the provisions of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1546" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1546">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1546</a>. The aim of NTM-I was to assist in the development of Iraqi security forces training structures and institutions so that Iraq can build an effective and sustainable capability that addresses the needs of the nation. NTM-I was not a combat mission but is a distinct mission, under the political control of NATO\'s North Atlantic Council. Its operational emphasis was on training and mentoring. The activities of the mission were coordinated with Iraqi authorities and the US-led Deputy Commanding General Advising and Training, who was also dual-hatted as the Commander of NTM-I. The mission officially concluded on 17 December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> invoked the first Article 4 meetings in 2003 at the start of the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>. Turkey also invoked this article twice in 2012 during the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/June_2012_interception_of_Turkish_aircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="June 2012 interception of Turkish aircraft">downing</a> of an unarmed Turkish <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_F-4_Phantom_II" title="McDonnell Douglas F-4 Phantom II">F-4 reconnaissance jet</a>, and after a mortar was fired at Turkey from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and again in 2015 after threats by <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> to its territorial integrity.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gulf_of_Aden_anti-piracy">Gulf of Aden anti-piracy</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ocean_Shield" title="Operation Ocean Shield">Operation Ocean Shield</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A tall plume of black smoke rises from the blue ocean waters next to a large gray battleship and a small black inflatable boat." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg/220px-Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg/330px-Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg/440px-Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gulf_of_Aden_-_disabled_pirate_boat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/USS_Farragut_(DDG-99)" title="USS Farragut (DDG-99)">USS <i>Farragut</i></a> destroying a Somali pirate skiff in March 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>Beginning on 17 August 2009, NATO deployed warships in an operation to protect maritime traffic in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a> and the Indian Ocean from <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Piracy in Somalia">Somali pirates</a>, and help strengthen the navies and coast guards of regional states. The operation was  approved by the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Council" title="North Atlantic Council">North Atlantic Council</a> and involves warships primarily from the United States though vessels from many other nations are also included. Operation <i>Ocean Shield</i> focuses on protecting the ships of Operation <i>Allied Provider</i> which are distributing aid as part of the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> mission in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> have sent warships to participate in the activities as well.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The operation seeks to dissuade and interrupt pirate attacks, protect vessels, and abetting to increase the general level of security in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libya_intervention">Libya intervention</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">2011 military intervention in Libya</a></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Civil_War_(2011)" title="Libyan Civil War (2011)">Libyan Civil War</a>, violence between protestors and the Libyan government under Colonel <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a> escalated, and on 17 March 2011 led to the passage of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973</a>, which called for a ceasefire, and authorized military action to protect civilians. A&#160;coalition that included several NATO members began enforcing a no-fly zone over Libya shortly afterwards, beginning with <a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ration_Harmattan" title="Op\xc3\xa9ration Harmattan">Op\xc3\xa9ration Harmattan</a> by the <a href="/wiki/French_Air_Force" title="French Air Force">French Air Force</a> on March 19.\n</p><p>On 20 March 2011, NATO states agreed on enforcing an arms embargo against Libya with <a href="/wiki/Operation_Unified_Protector" title="Operation Unified Protector">Operation <i>Unified Protector</i></a> using ships from NATO <a href="/wiki/Standing_NRF_Maritime_Group_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Standing NRF Maritime Group 1">Standing Maritime Group&#160;1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standing_NRF_Mine_Countermeasures_Group_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Standing NRF Mine Countermeasures Group 1">Standing Mine Countermeasures Group&#160;1</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NATOSecGen1_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NATOSecGen1-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and additional ships and submarines from NATO members.<sup id="cite_ref-NATOPressBriefing1_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NATOPressBriefing1-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> They would "monitor, report and, if needed, <a href="/wiki/Interdiction" title="Interdiction">interdict</a> vessels suspected of carrying illegal arms or <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenaries</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-NATOSecGen1_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NATOSecGen1-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Pieces of a destroyed tank, notably the gun turret, lie on a sandy landscape." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg/220px-Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg/330px-Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg/440px-Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="963" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmaria_bengasi_1903_0612_b1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Libyan Army <a href="/wiki/Palmaria_(artillery)" title="Palmaria (artillery)">Palmaria howitzers</a> destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/French_Air_Force" title="French Air Force">French Air Force</a> near <a href="/wiki/Benghazi" title="Benghazi">Benghazi</a> in March 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>On 24 March, NATO agreed to take control of the no-fly zone from the initial coalition, while command of targeting ground units remained with the coalition\'s forces.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> NATO began officially enforcing the UN resolution on 27 March 2011 with assistance from <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> By June, reports of divisions within the alliance surfaced as only eight of the 28 member nations were participating in combat operations,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> resulting in a confrontation between US Defense Secretary <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gates" title="Robert Gates">Robert Gates</a> and countries such as Poland, Spain, the Netherlands, Turkey, and Germany to contribute more, the latter believing the organization has overstepped its mandate in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In his final policy speech in Brussels on 10 June, Gates further criticized allied countries in suggesting their actions could cause the demise of NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The German foreign ministry pointed to "a&#160;considerable [German] contribution to NATO and NATO-led operations" and to the fact that this engagement was highly valued by President Obama.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the mission was extended into September, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> that day announced it would begin scaling down contributions and complete withdrawal by 1 August.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Earlier that week it was reported <a href="/wiki/Royal_Danish_Air_Force" title="Royal Danish Air Force">Danish air fighters</a> were running out of bombs.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The following week, the head of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> said the country\'s operations in the conflict were not sustainable.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the mission in October 2011, after the death of Colonel Gaddafi, NATO planes had flown about 9,500 strike sorties against pro-Gaddafi targets.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> A report from the organization <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> in May 2012 identified at least 72 civilians killed in the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\nFollowing a <a href="/wiki/2013_Libyan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2013 Libyan coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat attempt">coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat attempt</a> in October 2013, Libyan Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ali_Zeidan" title="Ali Zeidan">Ali Zeidan</a> requested technical advice and trainers from NATO to assist with ongoing security issues.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_countries">Participating countries</span></h2>\n<table style="background:white; border:1px solid rgb(153, 153, 153); margin: 1em auto 1em auto; overflow:auto; overflow-x:auto; overflow-y:hidden;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Map of title="Iraq">Iraq</a></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/23px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png" width="23" href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Members">Members</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO" title="Member states of NATO">Member states of NATO</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Twelve men in black suits stand talking in small groups under a backdrop with the words Lisbonne and Lisboa." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg/220px-NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg/330px-NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg/440px-NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="654" data-file-height="436" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NATO organizes regular summits for leaders of their members states and partnerships.</div></div></div>\n<p>NATO has twenty-nine members, mainly in Europe and North America. Some of these countries also have territory on multiple continents, which can be covered only as far south as the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a> in  the Atlantic Ocean, which defines NATO\'s "area of responsibility" under Article 6 of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a>. During the original treaty negotiations, the United States insisted that colonies such as the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a> be excluded from the treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins2011122\xe2\x80\x93123_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins2011122\xe2\x80\x93123-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">French Algeria</a> was however covered until <a href="/wiki/Algerian_independence_referendum,_1962" title="Algerian independence referendum, 1962">their independence</a> on 3 July 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Twelve of these twenty-nine are original members who joined in 1949, while the other seventeen joined in one of seven enlargement rounds.\n</p><p>From the mid-1960s to the mid-1990s, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> pursued a military strategy of independence from NATO under a policy dubbed "Gaullo-Mitterrandism".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> negotiated the return of France to the integrated military command and the Defence Planning Committee in 2009, the latter being disbanded the following year. France remains the only NATO member outside the Nuclear Planning Group and unlike the United States and the United Kingdom, will not commit its nuclear-armed submarines to the alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-WP-France_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-France-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-france_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-france-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Few members spend more than two percent of their gross domestic product on defence,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> with the United States accounting for three quarters of NATO defense spending.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlargement">Enlargement</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO" title="Enlargement of NATO">Enlargement of NATO</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg" class="image"><img alt="A map of Europe with countries labeled in shades of blue, green, and yellow based on when they joined NATO." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg/220px-History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg.png" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg/330px-History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg/440px-History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NATO has added 13 new members since the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> and the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>New membership in the alliance has been largely from <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>, including former members of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>. Accession to the alliance is governed with individual <a href="/wiki/Membership_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Membership Action Plan">Membership Action Plans</a>, and requires approval by each current member. NATO currently has two candidate countries that are in the process of joining the alliance: <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>.\nIn NATO official statements, the Republic of Macedonia is always referred to as the "former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia", with a footnote stating that "Turkey recognizes the Republic of Macedonia under its constitutional name". Though Macedonia completed its requirements for membership at the same time as <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, who joined NATO in 2009, its accession was blocked by Greece pending a resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">Macedonia naming dispute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In order to support each other in the process, new and potential members in the region formed the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Charter" title="Adriatic Charter">Adriatic Charter</a> in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> was also named as an aspiring member, and was promised "future membership" during the 2008 summit in Bucharest,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> though in 2014, US President Barack Obama said the country was not "currently on a path" to membership.<sup id="cite_ref-Obama_says_no_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Obama_says_no-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Russia continues to oppose further expansion, seeing it as inconsistent with informal understandings between Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> and European and American negotiators that allowed for a peaceful German reunification.<sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel_review_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel_review-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> NATO\'s expansion efforts are often seen by Moscow leaders as a continuation of a Cold War attempt to surround and isolate Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> though they have also been criticised in the West.<sup id="cite_ref-Art1998_383_to_384_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Art1998_383_to_384-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> A June 2016 <a href="/wiki/Levada_Center" title="Levada Center">Levada</a> poll found that 68% of Russians think that deploying NATO troops in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> \xe2\x80\x93 former Eastern bloc countries bordering Russia \xe2\x80\x93 is a threat to Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In contrast 65% of Poles surveyed in 2017 Pew Research Center report identified Russia as a "major threat", with an average of 31% saying so across all NATO countries<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>, and 67% of Poles surveyed in 2018 favour US forces being based in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Of non-CIS Eastern European countries surveyed by Gallup in 2016, all but Serbia and Montenegro were more likely than not to view NATO as a protective alliance rather than a threat.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Ukraine\xe2\x80\x93NATO relations">relationship with NATO</a> and Europe has been politically controversial, and improvement of these relations was one of the goals of the "<a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a>" protests that saw the ousting of pro-Russian President <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> in 2014. In March 2014, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Arseniy_Yatsenyuk" title="Arseniy Yatsenyuk">Arseniy Yatsenyuk</a> reiterated the government\'s stance that Ukraine is not seeking NATO membership.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Ukraine\'s president subsequently signed a bill dropping his nation\'s nonaligned status in order to pursue NATO membership, but signaled that it would hold a referendum before seeking to join.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Ukraine is one of eight countries in Eastern Europe with an <a href="/wiki/Individual_Partnership_Action_Plan" title="Individual Partnership Action Plan">Individual Partnership Action Plan</a>. IPAPs began in 2002, and are open to countries that have the political will and ability to deepen their relationship with NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 2006 study in the journal <i>Security Studies</i> argued that NATO enlargement contributed to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_consolidation" title="Democratic consolidation">democratic consolidation</a> in Central and Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_NATO" title="Foreign relations of NATO">Foreign relations of NATO</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hundreds of soldiers in military uniforms stand behind a line on a tarmac with 14 flags held by individuals at the front." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg/220px-Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg/330px-Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg/440px-Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2504" data-file-height="1588" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Partnership for Peace conducts multinational military exercises like Cooperative Archer, which took place in Tblisi in July 2007 with 500 servicemen from four NATO members, eight PfP members, and Jordan, a Mediterranean Dialogue participant.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> (PfP) programme was established in 1994 and is based on individual bilateral relations between each partner country and NATO: each country may choose the extent of its participation.<sup id="cite_ref-pfp_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pfp-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Members include all current and former members of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a> (EAPC) was first established on 29 May 1997, and is a forum for regular coordination, consultation and dialogue between all fifty participants.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>  The PfP programme is considered the operational wing of the Euro-Atlantic Partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-pfp_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pfp-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Other third countries also have been contacted for participation in some activities of the PfP framework such as Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) signed a comprehensive package of arrangements with NATO under the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Plus_agreement" title="Berlin Plus agreement">Berlin Plus agreement</a> on 16 December 2002. With this agreement, the EU was given the possibility to use NATO assets in case it wanted to act independently in an international crisis, on the condition that NATO itself did not want to act \xe2\x80\x93 the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Right_of_first_refusal" title="Right of first refusal">right of first refusal</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> For example, Article 42(7) of the 1982 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> specifies that "If a Member State is the victim of armed aggression on its territory, the other Member States shall have towards it an obligation of aid and assistance by all the means in their power". The treaty applies globally to specified territories whereas NATO is restricted under its Article 6 to operations north of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>. It provides a "double framework" for the EU countries that are also linked with the PfP programme.\n</p><p>Additionally, NATO cooperates and discusses its activities with numerous other non-NATO members. The <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Dialogue" title="Mediterranean Dialogue">Mediterranean Dialogue</a> was established in 1994 to coordinate in a similar way with <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Israel" title="Foreign relations of Israel">Israel</a> and countries in North Africa. The <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Cooperation_Initiative" title="Istanbul Cooperation Initiative">Istanbul Cooperation Initiative</a> was announced in 2004 as a dialog forum for the Middle East along the same lines as the Mediterranean Dialogue. The four participants are also linked through the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Political dialogue with Japan began in 1990, and since then, the Alliance has gradually increased its contact with countries that do not form part of any of these cooperation initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, NATO established a set of general guidelines that do not allow for a formal institutionalisation of relations, but reflect the Allies\' desire to increase cooperation. Following extensive debate, the term "Contact Countries" was agreed by the Allies in 2000. By 2012, the Alliance had broadened this group, which meets to discuss issues such as counter-piracy and technology exchange, under the names "partners across the globe" or "global partners".<sup id="cite_ref-gao_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gao-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, both contact countries, are also members of the <a href="/wiki/AUSCANNZUKUS" title="AUSCANNZUKUS">AUSCANNZUKUS</a> strategic alliance, and similar regional or bilateral agreements between contact countries and NATO members also aid cooperation. <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_NATO#Colombia" title="Foreign relations of NATO">Colombia</a> is the NATO\xe2\x80\x99s latest partner and Colombia has access to the full range of cooperative activities NATO offers to partners; <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> became the first and only <a href="/wiki/Latin_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin American">Latin American</a> country to cooperate with NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Structure_of_NATO" title="Structure of NATO">Structure of NATO</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/220px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/330px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/440px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3683" data-file-height="2037" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The North Atlantic Council convening in 2010 with a defence/foreign minister configuration</div></div></div>\n<p>All agencies and organizations of NATO integrated into either the civilian administrative or military executive roles. For the most part they perform roles and functions that directly or indirectly support the security role of the alliance as a whole.\n</p><p>The civilian structure includes:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <b><a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Council" title="North Atlantic Council">North Atlantic Council</a></b> (<b>NAC</b>) is the body which has effective governance authority and powers of decision in NATO, consisting of member states\' permanent representatives or representatives at higher level (ministers of foreign affairs or defence, or heads of state or government). The NAC convenes at least once a week and takes major decisions regarding NATO\'s policies. The meetings of the North Atlantic Council are chaired by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_NATO" title="Secretary General of NATO">Secretary General</a> and, when decisions have to be made, action is agreed upon on the basis of unanimity and common accord. There is no voting or decision by majority. Each nation represented at the Council table or on any of its subordinate committees retains complete sovereignty and responsibility for its own decisions.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/NATO_Headquarters" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Headquarters">NATO Headquarters</a></b>, located on Boulevard L\xc3\xa9opold&#160;III/Leopold III-laan, B-1110 Brussels, which is in <a href="/wiki/Haren,_Belgium" title="Haren, Belgium">Haren</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_(municipality)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels (municipality)">City of Brussels</a> municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The staff at the Headquarters is composed of national delegations of member countries and includes civilian and military liaison offices and officers or diplomatic missions and diplomats of partner countries, as well as the International Staff and International Military Staff filled from serving members of the armed forces of member states.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Non-governmental citizens\' groups have also grown up in support of NATO, broadly under the banner of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Council" title="Atlantic Council">Atlantic Council</a>/<a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Treaty_Association" title="Atlantic Treaty Association">Atlantic Treaty Association</a> movement.</li></ul>\n<div class="noviewer thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px"><div style="position:relative;width:450px;border:1px solid lightgray"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_laea_location_map.svg" class="image" title="NATO is located in NATO"><img alt="NATO is located in NATO" style="position:absolute;top:29.654%;left:76.15%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="School"
