data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:75%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:5px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px"><a href="/wiki/NATO_School" title="NATO School">School</a></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_laea_location_map.svg" title="File:NATO laea location map.svg"> </a></div>Locations of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">NATO</a>\'s two strategic commands \xe2\x80\x94 <a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Transformation" title="Allied Command Transformation">Allied Command Transformation</a> (ACT; yellow marks) and <a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Operations" title="Allied Command Operations">Allied Command Operations</a> (ACO; red marks) \xe2\x80\x94 the latter of which has <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Powers_Europe" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe">Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe</a> (SHAPE) as its headquarters. The subordinate centres of ACT and subordinate commands and joint force operational headquarters of ACO are also shown. <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:NATO_commands" title="Template:NATO commands"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:NATO_commands" title="Template talk:NATO commands"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:NATO_commands&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The military structure includes:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <b><a href="/wiki/NATO_Military_Committee" title="NATO Military Committee">Military Committee</a></b> (<b>MC</b>) is the body of NATO that is composed of <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO" title="Member states of NATO">member states</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Defence" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief of Defence">Chiefs of Defence</a> (CHOD) and advises the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Council" title="North Atlantic Council">North Atlantic Council</a> (NAC) on military policy and strategy. The national CHODs are regularly represented in the MC by their permanent Military Representatives (MilRep), who often are two- or three-star flag officers. Like the Council, from time to time the Military Committee also meets at a higher level, namely at the level of <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_defence" title="Chief of defence">Chiefs of Defence</a>, the most senior military officer in each nation\'s armed forces. The MC is led by its <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_NATO_Military_Committee" title="Chairman of the NATO Military Committee">chairman</a>, who directs NATO\'s military operations. Like the Council, from time to time the Military Committee also meets at a higher level, namely at the level of Chiefs of Defence, the most senior military officer in each nation\'s armed forces. Until 2008 the Military Committee excluded France, due to that country\'s 1966 decision to remove itself from the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Military_Command_Structure" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Military Command Structure">NATO Military Command Structure</a>, which it rejoined in 1995. Until France rejoined NATO, it was not represented on the Defence Planning Committee, and this led to conflicts between it and NATO members.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Such was the case in the lead up to <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Operation <i>Iraqi Freedom</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The operational work of the Committee is supported by the International Military Staff</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Powers_Europe" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe">Allied Command Operations</a></b> (<b>ACO</b>) is the NATO command of responsible for NATO operations worldwide.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Transformation" title="Allied Command Transformation">Allied Command Transformation</a></b> (<b>ACT</b>), responsible for transformation and training of NATO forces.</li>\n<li>The <b>Rapid Deployable Corps</b> include <a href="/wiki/Eurocorps" title="Eurocorps">Eurocorps</a>, <a href="/wiki/I._German/Dutch_Corps" title="I. German/Dutch Corps">I. German/Dutch Corps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multinational_Corps_Northeast" title="Multinational Corps Northeast">Multinational Corps Northeast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NATO_Rapid_Deployable_Italian_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Rapid Deployable Italian Corps">NATO Rapid Deployable Italian Corps</a> among others, as well as naval High Readiness Forces (HRFs), which all report to Allied Command Operations.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The organizations and agencies of NATO include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Headquarters for the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Support_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Support Agency">NATO Support Agency</a> will be in Capellen Luxembourg (site of the current NATO Maintenance and Supply Agency \xe2\x80\x93 NAMSA).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/NATO_Communications_and_Information_Agency" title="NATO Communications and Information Agency">NATO Communications and Information Agency</a> Headquarters will be in Brussels, as will the very small staff which will design the new NATO Procurement Agency.</li>\n<li>A new NATO Science and Technology (S&amp;T) Organization will be created before July 2012, consisting of Chief Scientist, a Programme Office for Collaborative S&amp;T, and the NATO Undersea Research Centre (NURC).</li>\n<li>The current <a href="/wiki/NATO_Standardization_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Standardization Agency">NATO Standardization Agency</a> will continue and be subject to review by Spring 2014.</li></ul>\n<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/NATO_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="NATO Parliamentary Assembly">NATO Parliamentary Assembly</a></b> (<b>NATO PA</b>) is a body that sets broad strategic goals for NATO, which meets at two session per year. NATO PA interacts directly with the parliamentary structures of the national governments of the member states which appoint Permanent Members, or ambassadors to NATO. The NATO Parliamentary Assembly is made up of legislators from the member countries of the North Atlantic Alliance as well as thirteen associate members. It is however officially a different structure from NATO, and has as aim to join together deputies of NATO countries in order to discuss security policies on the NATO Council.\n</p>\n<h2><span reading</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Asmus" title="Ronald Asmus">Asmus, Ronald</a> (2010). <i>A Little War That Shook the World: Georgia, Russia, and the Future of the West</i>. NYU. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-230-61773-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-230-61773-5">978-0-230-61773-5</a>.</li></ul>\n<ul><li>John Borawski, Thomas-Durell Young, NATO After 2000: The Future of the Euro-Atlantic Alliance</li>\n<li>Dr. Thomas-Durell Young, Reforming NATO\'s Military Structures: The Long-Term Study and Its Implications for Land Forces, Strategic Studies Institute, May 1, 1998.  Often taken for granted, the Alliance\'s integrated command structure provides the basis for NATO\'s collective defense, and increasingly, as seen in Bosnia, its ability to undertake peace support operations. However, the very value by which nations hold the structure has resulted in a difficult and time-consuming reorganization process, which has produced only limited reforms.</li>\n<li>Dr. Thomas-Durell Young, Multinational Land Formations and NATO: Reforming Practices and Structures, Strategic Studies Institute, December 1, 1997. Reduced national force structures, new NATO roles and missions emanating from the military implementation of Alliance Strategy and the rapid reaction requirements associated with the embryonic Combined Joint Task Forces (CJTF) concept are but three of a multitude of inter-related issues.</li>\n<li>The current official reference for the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Military_Command_Structure" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Military Command Structure">NATO Military Command Structure</a> appears to be MC 324/1 (The NATO Military Command Structure, May 2004) and a successor MC 324/2. The previous issue was MC 324, issued on 6 January 1999.</li>\n<li>NATO Office of Information and Press, NATO Handbook&#160;: Fiftieth Anniversary Edition, NATO, Brussels, 1998\xe2\x80\x9399, Second Reprint, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/92-845-0134-2" title="Special:BookSources/92-845-0134-2">92-845-0134-2</a></li></ul>\n<ul><li><cite class="citation web"><a href="/wiki/Hastings_Ismay,_1st_Baron_Ismay" title="Hastings Ismay, 1st Baron Ismay">Hastings Ismay, 1st Baron Ismay</a> (1954). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://archives.nato.int/nato-first-5-years-1949-1954-by-lord-ismay-secretary-general-of-north-atlantic-treaty-organization;isad">"NATO: The First Five Years"</a>.
